# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repository:** `github.com/sg-evals/node--v22.13.0`
- Use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/node--v22.13.0$` filter in keyword_search
- Use `github.com/sg-evals/node--v22.13.0` as the `repo` parameter for go_to_definition/find_references/read_file


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Node.js CommonJS to ESM Module Loader Migration Surface

## Your Task

Find all JavaScript and C++ source files in nodejs/node that implement the ESM loader and CJS-ESM interop bridge. Identify: the ModuleLoader class (lib/internal/modules/esm/loader.js), the CJS loader's ESM fallback (finalizeEsmResolution in lib/internal/modules/cjs/loader.js), the ESM translators for different formats, the ESM specifier resolver, the ModuleJob linking/evaluation pipeline, the entry point ESM detection (run_main.js), and the native ModuleWrap C++ binding.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the migration domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/node--v22.13.0.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/node--v22.13.0` (nodejs/node)

Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive analysis of the Node.js ESM loader and CJS-ESM interop bridge implementation. Here's what I discovered:

## Summary

I identified **20 key files** implementing the ESM loader and CJS-ESM interop bridge:

### ESM Loader Core (lib/internal/modules/esm/)
- **loader.js** - `ModuleLoader` class orchestrating the entire loading pipeline
- **module_job.js** - `ModuleJob`/`ModuleJobSync` classes handling module linking, instantiation, and evaluation
- **translators.js** - Translator functions for different module formats (JS, JSON, WASM, TypeScript, etc.)
- **resolve.js** - `defaultResolve` and package resolution logic
- **load.js** - `defaultLoad` and source loading functions
- **hooks.js** - `HooksProxy` for custom user-provided loader hooks
- **module_map.js** - `ResolveCache` and `LoadCache` for caching
- **get_format.js** - Format detection logic
- **formats.js** - File extension and MIME type mappings
- **assert.js** - Import attribute validation
- **initialize_import_meta.js** - Sets up import.meta object
- **utils.js** - `compileSourceTextModule` bridge function
- Plus supporting files: shared_constants.js, fetch_module.js, create_dynamic_module.js, worker.js

### CJS-ESM Interop
- **lib/internal/modules/cjs/loader.js** - `finalizeEsmResolution` function for ESM resolution fallback in CommonJS

### Entry Point Detection
- **lib/internal/modules/run_main.js** - `shouldUseESMLoader` determines if main should be ESM

### Native Binding
- **src/module_wrap.cc/h** - C++ `ModuleWrap` class binding V8's module system to JavaScript

The answer.json file contains a complete mapping of these files, their key symbols, the execution chain, and a detailed narrative explaining how they work together.

functionality to the\\n158:    * `customizations` object, including registration, loading, and resolving.\\n159:    * There are some responsibilities that this class _always_ takes\\n160:    * care of, like validating outputs, so that the customizations object\\n161:    * does not have to do so.\\n162:    *\\n163:    * The customizations object has the shape:\\n164:    *\\n165:    * ```ts\\n166:
